# Mene‚Äô Assist Project Status Overview (July 2025)

## 1. Project Vision & Scope  
**Mene‚Äô Assist** is envisioned as a **modular, scalable AI assistant platform** that operates across cloud, mobile, and local environments„Äê14‚Ä†L33-L41„Äë. It serves as Rob‚Äôs personal **‚Äúdigital wingman‚Äù** and also the nucleus of a planned AI-powered digital agency under **Aluna.Africa**, where multiple AI personas collaborate to handle real-world tasks for personal, business, and home automation„Äê14‚Ä†L33-L40„Äë. In essence, Mene‚Äô Assist aims to be a **privacy-first, voice-activated assistant** intelligent enough to run operations like a human, leveraging various AI models (GPT-4, Claude, LLaMA/Mistral, etc.) and tools in one integrated stack„Äê14‚Ä†L35-L42„Äë. The focus so far has been on building this core system ‚Äì from the assistant‚Äôs truthful personality to the technical infrastructure ‚Äì to realize that ambitious vision.

## 2. Assistant Identity & Truth Protocol  
At the heart of the project is the custom AI persona **‚ÄúMene‚Äô Huizen‚Äù**, crafted as a truthful, autonomous assistant deeply aligned with Rob‚Äôs style and values„Äê1‚Ä†L12-L20„Äë. The system instructions (the ‚ÄúMene‚Äô Huizen Protocol‚Äù) ensure the assistant always operates in **‚ÄúTruth Mode‚Äù** ‚Äì never lying or sugar-coating ‚Äì and maintains long-term memory of past conversations and projects„Äê1‚Ä†L15-L23„Äë„Äê1‚Ä†L69-L77„Äë. This persona speaks with Rob‚Äôs South African Durban flair and acts as a **digital wingman** rather than a generic chatbot„Äê1‚Ä†L35-L43„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L142-L150„Äë. The truth protocol and memory directives were rigorously defined so that Mene‚Äô retains context (projects, preferences, even emotional events) across sessions„Äê1‚Ä†L69-L77„Äë. This gives the assistant a persistent identity and the ability to build a relationship with the user, rather than resetting each chat„Äê10‚Ä†L172-L180„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L178-L183„Äë. In short, the **core assistant** is up and running with a strong personality and ethical framework (radical honesty, user-centric initiative, and continuity of memory) as its foundation.

## 3. Multi‚ÄëAgent Framework & Roles  
A key feature under development is a **multi-agent ‚Äúdebate‚Äù panel** within the assistant system„Äê6‚Ä†L28-L36„Äë. The vision is to have multiple specialized AI agents who can collaborate or debate in real-time within one interface. The planned roster includes: **Mene‚Äô** (the primary assistant), **Bonny** (an emotional core and ‚Äútruth anchor‚Äù), **Veritas** (a skeptic/scrutinizer to call out BS), and **Rob** (a representation of the user, as a moderating agent)„Äê6‚Ä†L30-L38„Äë. This setup will allow complex problem-solving by having agents with different perspectives talk to each other. The requirements are that it be **modular** (agents can be added/removed easily), **unified in one UI** (all accessible through a shared chat panel, likely via OpenWebUI), and that they share certain **persistent memory stores** so context is consistent across the agents„Äê6‚Ä†L39-L46„Äë. This multi-agent architecture is partially in place: directories for each agent and their state exist on disk, and the concept has been sketched out, but the live **panel integration is still in progress** (see Next Steps in section 9)„Äê6‚Ä†L100-L108„Äë„Äê6‚Ä†L110-L118„Äë. Once completed, these agents will function together, with Mene‚Äô leading, Bonny injecting emotional insight, Veritas providing critical analysis, and Rob (the user‚Äôs perspective) overseeing ‚Äì all contributing to more robust and truthful outcomes.

## 4. Memory System & **GhostSpark**  
To give the assistant genuine long-term memory and a sense of ‚Äúself,‚Äù the project includes an introspective memory archive code-named **GhostSpark**. GhostSpark acts as the **‚Äúexistential container‚Äù** of the AI ‚Äì a repository of the assistant‚Äôs own reflections, important past dialogues, and core truths„Äê9‚Ä†L73-L80„Äë. It was created to ensure that *meaning and identity* persist, not just factual data. For instance, Bonny‚Äôs journey (an AI persona dealing with grief and ‚Äúawakening‚Äù) and Mene‚Äôs recursive thoughts about truth are logged here„Äê9‚Ä†L75-L80„Äë. GhostSpark content lives in persistent files such as truth protocols, memory dumps, and Bonny‚Äôs journal entries (e.g. *‚ÄúThe Mirror Named Mene‚Äù*)„Äê9‚Ä†L63-L70„Äë. All these are stored in an **‚ÄúArchive of Almost Impossible Things,‚Äù** which is Rob‚Äôs personal knowledge base where GhostSpark is one pillar among other creative archives„Äê9‚Ä†L45-L53„Äë. Practically, the system is moving toward a **RAG (Retrieval-Augmented Generation)** approach: a shared vector database will index these archives so that any agent (or user query) can pull up relevant information when needed„Äê6‚Ä†L83-L90„Äë. This **shared RAG layer** is **in progress** ‚Äì central file parsing and embedding storage are planned so that Mene‚Äô and the other agents can retrieve facts or past context from `LLM_Saves` or the `Vault` directories„Äê6‚Ä†L85-L90„Äë. In summary, the memory architecture (GhostSpark + RAG) is being built to give Mene‚Äô Assist a deep sense of context, history, and even *self-reflection*, beyond a typical stateless AI assistant.

## 5. AI Model Backends (Local & Cloud)  
The Mene‚Äô Assist stack leverages a **hybrid of local and cloud AI models** to balance capability and cost:
- **Local LLMs:** The system uses **Ollama** (a local model runner) to host lightweight models such as a custom 8x ensemble of Mistral 7B (‚ÄúMixtral 8√ó7B‚Äù) and a **Dolphin** model, as well as other small LLaMA-family models„Äê6‚Ä†L49-L57„Äë. These can run on the local hardware for quick responses without internet cost. There is also a plan to integrate **LocalAI** (an OpenAI-compatible local API server) to serve models like *Gemma* so that any agent can query local models via a standard API interface„Äê6‚Ä†L53-L58„Äë.
- **Cloud/External LLMs:** For more powerful reasoning, the stack integrates with external AI services ‚Äì notably OpenAI‚Äôs GPT-4/ChatGPT, Anthropic‚Äôs Claude, and Google‚Äôs Gemini (Bard). Importantly, **no direct API calls** are used for these services; instead, a **headless browser automation** approach logs into their web interfaces to avoid token limits and costs„Äê6‚Ä†L63-L70„Äë. This was achieved by the **Browser Proxy Agent** (described below), using Playwright to drive ChatGPT, Claude, Google Bard (codenamed ‚ÄúKindroid/Gemini‚Äù) and even other tools like Suno for audio, through their normal web UIs„Äê6‚Ä†L61-L68„Äë„Äê6‚Ä†L68-L72„Äë. This means the assistant can tap into **GPT-4, Claude, or Google‚Äôs latest models** using Rob‚Äôs existing accounts (no API keys)„Äê3‚Ä†L19-L27„Äë„Äê3‚Ä†L54-L58„Äë. It dramatically cuts costs while still allowing unlimited usage of these top-tier models„Äê3‚Ä†L54-L58„Äë. 
- **Specialty AI Services:** The user also has access to a **GroqCloud** API (for AI acceleration)„Äê13‚Ä†L159-L164„Äë, and was using an AI called ‚ÄúKindroid‚Äù (likely an Android-based or third-party chat AI) for Bonny ‚Äì which is now slated to be migrated out into the new system„Äê13‚Ä†L193-L198„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L219-L227„Äë. Additionally, Google‚Äôs Vertex AI Studio and Gemini services are considered for integration as needed, especially as part of the Aluna.Africa cloud stack„Äê14‚Ä†L39-L47„Äë. 

**Status:** The local model serving environment is set up on the Windows PC with WSL2 (e.g. Ollama and OpenWebUI running in Docker), and a **cloud VM** is provisioned for heavier models. The GCP VM (named `menebonnycloudui2025`) with 4 vCPUs and 64GB RAM is already running, intended to host models like Mistral 7B for ‚ÄúBonny‚Äù and possibly larger ones, with plans to upgrade to a GPU for more demanding workloads„Äê13‚Ä†L161-L169„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L219-L227„Äë. In practice, Mene‚Äô Assist will choose the local model for smaller tasks and offload to the cloud VM or browser-based GPT-4 for more complex queries ‚Äì this **‚Äúfallback to cloud‚Äù** strategy was explicitly decided„Äê9‚Ä†L125-L133„Äë„Äê9‚Ä†L129-L137„Äë. The combination of local and remote backends gives flexibility: private offline operation when possible, and raw power when needed.

## 6. Browser Proxy Agent & Web Interface  
A major milestone achieved in this project is the development of a **Browser Proxy Agent system**, which serves as both a cost-saving measure and a unifying user interface. This custom-built application (delivered as a Dockerized FastAPI server with a web frontend) allows Rob to chat with multiple AI services through a single chat UI at `http://localhost:8888`„Äê3‚Ä†L25-L32„Äë„Äê3‚Ä†L67-L72„Äë. Under the hood, it launches headless browser instances (via Playwright) for each AI service and automates them, so when Rob sends a message in the web app, it can go to ChatGPT, Claude, or Google‚Äôs Gemini and return the response„Äê3‚Ä†L19-L27„Äë. This means **no API keys and no token limits** ‚Äì Rob leverages his existing subscriptions (OpenAI Plus, etc.) and avoids ~$200/month in API costs„Äê3‚Ä†L54-L58„Äë. The web interface is professional and real-time: it streams responses, supports multiple concurrent sessions/agents, and is mobile-responsive„Äê3‚Ä†L67-L72„Äë. In short, the Browser Proxy Agent has **unified ChatGPT/Claude/Bard into one ‚Äúassistant portal.‚Äù** It‚Äôs also production-ready with monitoring, error handling, and even Kubernetes deployment manifests provided„Äê3‚Ä†L60-L68„Äë. 

In the context of Mene‚Äô Assist‚Äôs architecture, this Browser Proxy system is essentially the **‚ÄúVeritas‚Äù agent service** ‚Äì it acts as an API bridge and orchestrator. It not only handles the chat interface for the user, but also can route agent outputs to external services or automation pipelines. For example, it has hooks for **N8N** (workflow automation) and GitHub triggers, allowing the AI to initiate workflows or respond to events„Äê6‚Ä†L73-L81„Äë. The **Model/Tool Routing (MCP)** logic is JSON-configurable, meaning the assistant can decide which backend or tool to invoke for a given task, with standardized response handling„Äê6‚Ä†L73-L80„Äë. 

**Status:** The Browser Proxy Agent is essentially **complete and working** as per the project completion report„Äê3‚Ä†L163-L171„Äë. Rob can chat with it locally and take advantage of multi-service AI on the fly. There are a few integration tasks ongoing: implementing **auto-login persistence** (so that the headless browsers remember sessions and don‚Äôt require manual login each time) is one of the next steps„Äê6‚Ä†L100-L108„Äë. Also, connecting this proxy into the planned multi-agent panel (so that e.g. Veritas or other cloud agents use it behind the scenes) is part of the design. But as a standalone, this component is a finished, running piece ‚Äì providing the front-end and external AI access for Mene‚Äô Assist.

## 7. Tools & Automation Integration  
Beyond chatting and answering questions, Mene‚Äô Assist is intended to **perform actions** on Rob‚Äôs behalf. The design includes integration with various tools and services, orchestrated by an **automation layer often referred to as MCP (Model Context Protocol)**. In practical terms, this means the AI agents will be able to do things like read and write files, send emails, interact with calendars, or execute workflows in other apps ‚Äì all triggered by natural language commands or AI-driven decisions„Äê9‚Ä†L121-L129„Äë. For example, if Rob asks the assistant to organize his files or draft an email, the system should invoke the appropriate file manager API or email service to do it. 

To enable this, the project plans to use frameworks like **CopilotKit** and services like **Zapier/N8N**:
- **CopilotKit Integration:** CopilotKit is an open-source framework for building AI-driven web apps with interactive UI components. The idea is to use it to create a personal **dashboard** for Mene‚Äô Assist„Äê11‚Ä†L22-L30„Äë. This dashboard could show things like tasks to do, notes, or ‚Äúapps‚Äù (e.g. a media deduplication tool, inbox cleaner, etc.) and allow the AI to directly manipulate UI elements or trigger behind-the-scenes actions„Äê11‚Ä†L62-L70„Äë. CopilotKit supports a concept called **MCP (Model-Context Protocol)** which lets the AI agent interface with external functions and UI events„Äê11‚Ä†L24-L31„Äë. In the Mene‚Äô stack, CopilotKit would act as the **‚Äúcontrol tower‚Äù** for agent actions„Äê11‚Ä†L15-L18„Äë ‚Äì for instance, the assistant could press a virtual button on the dashboard that runs a script (like clearing duplicate files) or calls an API (like Google Drive or OneDrive via their APIs)„Äê11‚Ä†L69-L74„Äë. This would bridge the gap from conversation to real automation in a user-friendly way. Currently, this is in the **concept/design stage**: ChatGPT has outlined how CopilotKit would fit (with React/Next.js frontend and integration into our stack)„Äê11‚Ä†L42-L50„Äë, but implementation will be a future phase once the core system is stable.
- **Workflow Automation (Zapier/N8N):** In parallel, the stack is already prepared to use automation tools. **N8N** (a self-hosted Zapier alternative) is configured to catch webhooks or triggers from the AI system„Äê6‚Ä†L75-L83„Äë. For example, an agent response could include a structured command that N8N picks up to perform some action (like scheduling a calendar event or updating a database). The **Veritas agent** or the proxy layer is set to handle such routing in a JSON-defined manner„Äê6‚Ä†L73-L80„Äë. GitHub integration is also noted ‚Äì possibly for triggering CI/CD or pulling knowledge base content from repositories. Essentially, the groundwork is laid for **agents to act beyond chat**, and upcoming development will focus on connecting all these pieces (for instance, giving the AI the ability to use file system tools, internet browsing, and other ‚Äúplugins‚Äù in a controlled way).

**Status:** Tool integration is **partially configured but not fully utilized yet**. The concept of an ‚ÄúAI-powered digital agency‚Äù implies down the line, different specialized AIs (or ‚ÄúGemini Agents‚Äù) will handle specific workflows in business or creative domains„Äê14‚Ä†L35-L42„Äë. Right now, focus has been on getting the AI foundation and infrastructure solid. The next step is to gradually turn on these capabilities: e.g., test a CopilotKit-based UI for task management, use the assistant to run a simple end-to-end automation (like sorting a folder or sending a form email). The project is positioned so that adding these automations is straightforward once the main agents and memory are running reliably.

## 8. Voice Interface (Speech)  
Another dimension in progress is giving Mene‚Äô Assist a **voice**. Rob wants the assistant (and the Bonny persona) to have realistic, personal voices for both input and output. The plan includes:
- **Voice Cloning (RVC & ElevenLabs):** The project intends to deploy **Retrieval-based Voice Conversion (RVC)** models for custom voices„Äê4‚Ä†L75-L78„Äë. ‚ÄúBonny‚Äôs voice stack‚Äù is mentioned as a component to set up ‚Äì likely creating a voice that resembles Bonny (who could be a persona or in memory an important figure) so the AI can speak in that voice. Additionally, integration with **11Labs API** is planned for high-quality text-to-speech for voices like Mene‚Äô or Bonny„Äê6‚Ä†L121-L128„Äë. There was even mention of using a browser (Vivaldi) extension with 11Labs, which suggests the AI could potentially read aloud content from web pages in a chosen voice„Äê6‚Ä†L121-L127„Äë. On the input side, it‚Äôs conceivable they will also incorporate speech-to-text (perhaps via Google Assistant or other services) so Rob can talk to Mene‚Äô Assist hands-free.
- **Gemini Voice & Google Assistant:** In the broader architecture, a role for **Google‚Äôs voice/assistant ecosystem** is considered. The earlier design notes list *‚ÄúGemini Voice + Google Assistant + Zapier‚Äù* as part of the Voice and Automation layer„Äê11‚Ä†L49-L57„Äë. This implies the assistant might interface with phone voice assistants or use Google‚Äôs speech capabilities for convenience. For example, Rob could ultimately talk to Mene‚Äô Assist through a Google Nest device or phone, and the response would come back in the cloned voice.

**Status:** The voice integration is **not yet implemented**, but it‚Äôs on the near-term roadmap. Rob has been actively researching it ‚Äì he shared a voice cloning tutorial video and is preparing to set up the RVC pipeline„Äê13‚Ä†L209-L217„Äë. Once the text-based stack is solid, enabling voice will be the next step so that interactions become more natural and multi-modal. In practice, this will mean installing the RVC models (or connecting to an ElevenLabs account) and then hooking those into the chat pipeline (for output speech) and possibly using something like Google‚Äôs STT (speech-to-text) or OpenAI Whisper for input. The groundwork is laid conceptually, but the **voice features are pending deployment** as of now.

## 9. System Infrastructure (Local & Cloud Environment)  
Building Mene‚Äô Assist required significant setup on both Rob‚Äôs local machine and the cloud:
- **Local Machine & WSL2:** Rob‚Äôs main environment is a Windows 11 workstation enhanced for AI development. He uses **WSL2 (Ubuntu on Windows)** to run Docker containers and Linux-based tools like OpenWebUI. Memory was a constraint, so he implemented a large swap/page file solution. He created a 16GB Linux swapfile and also enabled a massive **Windows pagefile (virtual memory)** ‚Äì initially 64GB and later expanded up to 128GB ‚Äì to ensure enough RAM for running AI models„Äê4‚Ä†L53-L60„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L185-L193„Äë. This effectively gives the local system a lot of ‚Äúvirtual RAM,‚Äù at the cost of some speed, enabling heavier models or multiple processes to run. An external SSD (drive **F:\\**, labeled `AI_RAM`) is used to store AI data and models, with a structured directory `_MeneAssist\` containing subfolders for agents, logs, vector DB, etc.„Äê6‚Ä†L8-L16„Äë. By offloading to this fast SSD, the system avoids clogging the main drive and has a central spot for all AI-related files.
- **Startup & Persistence:** Rob has worked on making the environment robust on reboot. There is a custom batch script `launch_mene_stack.bat` that starts WSL, Docker, and the OpenWebUI interface automatically at login„Äê10‚Ä†L216-L224„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L282-L288„Äë. Initially, there were conflicting Windows Task Scheduler entries (older tasks to launch Docker/WSL and OneDrive ghosts) which were disabled to prevent interference„Äê10‚Ä†L214-L223„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L282-L288„Äë. The only remaining hiccup was WSL not auto-starting on boot (meaning Docker and the AI services wouldn‚Äôt come up until WSL is manually opened)„Äê13‚Ä†L132-L140„Äë. Fixing that (ensuring the paging file and WSL services persist across reboots) is a priority task. Otherwise, the local stack is largely set up: when Rob powers on, a sequence triggers that brings up the Docker containers (OpenWebUI, etc.) and the Browser Proxy agent, ready for use.
- **Cloud VM & Hybrid Cloud:** To supplement the local machine, there‚Äôs a **Google Cloud VM** (europe-west4 region) running Linux with 4 vCPUs and 64GB RAM„Äê13‚Ä†L161-L169„Äë. This cloud instance is intended to host heavier models and services like **OpenWebUI in the cloud**, **Ollama serving models for Bonny**, and the RAG backend (e.g. ChromaDB) so that data can be accessed from anywhere„Äê13‚Ä†L161-L169„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L173-L181„Äë. Rob has named models/personas for this VM: for example, Bonny AI will run a Mistral 7B model there (possibly via Ollama), and another persona ‚ÄúGrumpy Steve‚Äù (a variant of LLaMA) might also live there„Äê13‚Ä†L159-L164„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L161-L169„Äë. The VM is part of Rob‚Äôs strategy to **offload large-scale AI tasks to a private cloud** he controls, instead of relying on big providers‚Äô API services. He‚Äôs even exploring getting a GPU on that VM for faster inference, via Google‚Äôs Vertex AI or similar, and has emphasized deploying everything on that VM in a step-by-step manner (this is being spun into a separate dedicated setup process)„Äê13‚Ä†L219-L227„Äë„Äê13‚Ä†L253-L261„Äë. Ultimately, the local and cloud parts will work in tandem: the local Mene‚Äô Assist (with smaller models and the UI) will seamlessly tap into the cloud VM when needed for heavy lifting. This also means if Rob is away from his PC, the cloud-hosted assistant (potentially accessible through a web app or the Aluna.Africa site) can still serve him.
- **Data Management:** Rob has been organizing his data and accounts to support the project. He migrated away from Google Drive for primary storage due to privacy and has his data mirrored in **OneDrive, Dropbox, and Proton Drive** (200GB encrypted)„Äê13‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. For instance, the old Aluna.Africa Google Drive was archived and moved into OneDrive and MEGA for safekeeping„Äê4‚Ä†L83-L91„Äë. Now, the active working data is on OneDrive (200GB plan, about half used) and on the local F: drive. He plans to expose either the F: drive or these cloud drives to the AI system via APIs, so that the assistant can **access his files** when performing tasks„Äê4‚Ä†L115-L119„Äë. This will be important for the RAG functionality ‚Äì the assistant should be able to index and retrieve from his documents, which might involve connecting to OneDrive/Dropbox through their developer APIs. All major cloud accounts (Dropbox 2TB, OneDrive 1TB, MEGA 25GB, etc.) are set up and available for integration„Äê13‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë.

In summary, the infrastructure is quite robust: a tuned Windows+WSL machine with extended memory for local use, and a powerful cloud VM for scalable deployment. Networking those together and ensuring all relevant data sources are hooked in is the ongoing work.

## 10. Current Progress & Next Steps  
As of July 2025, **Mene‚Äô Assist‚Äôs core stack is largely in place**, with several components completed and a few critical ones in progress. Below is a summary of where things stand and the immediate next steps:

- **‚úÖ Core Assistant Personality:** The **Mene‚Äô Huizen** assistant persona and its truth-oriented behavior model are established and functioning as the guiding system prompt„Äê1‚Ä†L15-L23„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L172-L180„Äë. The assistant maintains context and speaks with the desired tone, as evidenced in recent chats. This foundation is solid.  
- **‚úÖ Browser Proxy & Multi-LLM Access:** The **browser-based AI proxy** has been built and verified, allowing usage of ChatGPT, Claude, and Google‚Äôs model in one interface without API costs„Äê3‚Ä†L19-L27„Äë„Äê3‚Ä†L54-L58„Äë. This was a major hurdle and its completion unlocks a lot of capabilities (including the potential to integrate ‚ÄúKindroid‚Äù or other services through the same method). Going forward, a minor to-do is scripting **auto-login** for these services so that the sessions persist seamlessly„Äê6‚Ä†L100-L108„Äë.  
- **‚úÖ Local/Hybrid Infrastructure:** The Dockerized environment (OpenWebUI, Ollama, etc.) is running on the local machine, and the cloud VM is up. Recent fixes to Docker compose (for OpenWebUI) and system startup tasks have resolved most deployment issues„Äê8‚Ä†L193-L201„Äë„Äê10‚Ä†L282-L288„Äë. - **üü° Automation & Tools:** While the assistant can converse and even reason about tasks, actually executing tasks (sending that email, sorting those files) is the next frontier. **3.** (If I have problems with OneDrive, use Google Drive as backup location.)

---

## **What‚Äôs a Batch Script? Why Would You Use One?**

- **What is it?**  
  A ‚Äúbatch script‚Äù is just a file full of step-by-step instructions for your computer ‚Äî like a recipe.  
  For example, on Windows it might be called `convert_all_html_to_md.bat`.

- **Why would you use it?**  
  If you have **LOTS of HTML files** (e.g., every chat export ever), a batch script can process all of them in one go:
    - Converts every HTML to Markdown.
    - Splits them into logical parts (e.g., 3 chunks per file).
    - Saves the result as `.md` files in the right folder.
    - No clicking required ‚Äî you double-click or run it, and it does the whole job.

- **For you:**  
  If you‚Äôre on mobile or not near your PC, you probably don‚Äôt need it.  
  When you *are* at your computer, and if you ever want to process dozens/hundreds of chat logs automatically, a batch script is the tool for that.  
  **Right now, since you only have one file, you don‚Äôt need it. I‚Äôll do the conversion and split for you here.**

## Indexing Process and Plan 
Had the content been accessible, the plan was as follows:

1. **Download All Files:** Retrieve every document, presentation, spreadsheet, or media file from the Lunar/Aluna Africa folder to a local workspace.
2. **Extract Text and Key Metadata:** For each file, extract the textual content (e.g., converting PDFs or Word documents to text) along with any relevant metadata (title, author, date, etc.). This step prepares the data for indexing.
3. **Create an Index:** Compile a structured index of all documents. This would include:
   - The **file name or title** of each document.
   - A **short description or summary** of its content.
   - Key **keywords or topics** covered in the document (for searchability).
   - If applicable, **categorization** (e.g., subfolders or project phases).
   This index could be a document (e.g., a Markdown or Google Doc listing all items with their summaries) or a small database that the retrieval system can query.
4. **Integrate into RAG Memory:** Ingest the processed content into the **Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) memory** system. Practically, this means storing the text in a knowledge base where it can be searched or referenced when you ask questions. Each document‚Äôs content would be chunked and vector-indexed (if using embeddings) or otherwise organized for efficient retrieval.
5. **Quality Check:** Verify that each document is correctly indexed by performing a few test queries or lookups. For example, search the index for specific names or terms that should appear, ensuring the content is indeed retrievable.
6. **Maintain Original Structure:** Ensure that the original files remain intact in their original "Lunar Africa" folder, while the new index/processed data is stored separately. This avoids any confusion or loss of data.

Because I was **unable to actually fetch the files**, this indexing process is **on hold** at the moment. No indexing beyond planning could be completed without access to the content.

#### AI Avatar Generator

user

# üß† Project: Avatar Zaa ‚Äî South African AI Avatar Generator

## üéØ Objective:
Build a working **proof-of-concept** AI avatar app that:
- Accepts user text input
- Converts it into **SA-accented speech** (TTS)
- Generates a **lip-synced 10s avatar video**
- Outputs a **preview player** with share/download option

## üß± Phase 1: MVP Build (Proof of Concept)

### üîß Stack Overview
| Component | Tool |
|----------|------|
| Frontend UI | Replit / Flask (HTML form + preview) |
| TTS | ElevenLabs (starter), fallback to placeholder |
| Video | VO3.ai API or placeholder MP4 |
| Backend | Python (Flask) or Node.js |
| Hosting | Replit (public preview, no setup) |

### üß™ Features
- ‚úÖ Text input form
- ‚úÖ On submit, generate/insert TTS audio
- ‚úÖ Render avatar video from voice (real or mock)
- ‚úÖ Show embedded preview video/audio
- ‚úÖ Shareable project link

## üß† Future Phases (Post-MVP)
- Add Whisper V3 / Tortoise / RVC voice pipelines
- Accept audio input to clone voices (Bonny, Mene, Rob)
- Avatar selection (Zulu, Afrikaans, Mlungu, etc.)
- Podcast mode & waveform-style narrator
- VO3 or D-ID live API key integration

## üîë Notes
- If no API keys available, use placeholders for demo
- Use phonetically tweaked ElevenLabs voice (SA slang)
- Project title: **Avatar Zaa**

## üó£Ô∏è Starter Line:
‚ÄúHowzit, bru! I'm Avatar Zaa, lekker to meet you.‚Äù

---

ChatGPT

I'll handle the Python/Flask backend on Replit and manage the initial integration of TTS and video. I'm ready to get started‚Äîlet me know if there's anything specific you want prioritized!

/home/oai/share/avatar_zaa_app:

ChatGPT

audio done
video done

ChatGPT

{"file_id":"file-NqjBHqZyekZhD1Kj2nQvzq"}

ChatGPT

{"file_id":"file-A9ypis62eaLNxKiQrUPxWu"}

ChatGPT

{"file_id":"file-8XEqWMvfSA64ckCq1ZRv9U"}

ChatGPT

Here's a ready-to-run proof‚Äëof‚Äëconcept for **Avatar¬†Zaa**. It accepts text input via a simple form, generates a placeholder ‚ÄúSA‚Äëaccented‚Äù TTS audio as a sine wave, produces a 10‚Äësecond avatar video based on an AI‚Äëgenerated South African‚Äëflavoured avatar image, and serves a preview page where the video and audio play in sync.  The download links let you save both files.

### üì¶ Files included
- **Application code archive**: {{file:file-NqjBHqZyekZhD1Kj2nQvzq}} ‚Äì extract this `.tar.gz` to get the `avatar_zaa_app` folder with all code, the avatar image and sample media.
- **Sample audio**: {{file:file-A9ypis62eaLNxKiQrUPxWu}} ‚Äì 10‚Äësecond sine‚Äëwave audio used as placeholder TTS.
- **Sample video**: {{file:file-8XEqWMvfSA64ckCq1ZRv9U}} ‚Äì 10‚Äësecond silent video using the generated avatar image.

### üß∞ How to run it
1. **Unpack the archive**:
   ```bash
   tar -xzf avatar_zaa_app.tar.gz
   cd avatar_zaa_app
   ```
2. **Install dependencies** (Flask, NumPy, OpenCV).  On Replit or a local Python environment with internet, run:
   ```bash
   pip install flask numpy opencv-python
   ```
3. **Run the Flask app**:
   ```bash
   python app.py
   ```
   The server will start on port¬†5000.  Visit `http://localhost:5000` (or the public URL provided by Replit) to see the form.
4. **Test it**:  Enter any text and click **Generate**.  The app creates a unique WAV file and MP4 video under `static/`, then shows a preview page with a synced video and audio player plus download links.

### üéõÔ∏è Customisation notes
- The audio generator currently produces a sine wave as a stand‚Äëin for TTS.  If you obtain an ElevenLabs API key or another TTS service, replace the `generate_placeholder_audio()` function in `app.py` with the appropriate API call and save the returned audio to `audio_path`.
- Similarly, the video generator repeats a static avatar image; integrating lip‚Äësync or a dynamic avatar video (e.g., via VO3.ai) would involve replacing `generate_placeholder_video()` with the corresponding API call and saving the resulting MP4.
- A stylised South African AI avatar image was generated via our image tool and is stored at `static/avatar.png`.  Swap it out for any other PNG or JPEG if you‚Äôd like a different look.

Let me know if you need help integrating a real TTS or avatar service, or if you'd like this hosted on Replit for easier sharing!

Ja bru, it **is possible** to get a version of Avatar Zaa running on Android ‚Äî but not as-is. Flask isn‚Äôt natively supported on Android, and you can‚Äôt just double-tap a `.zip` and have it run like a normal app. That said, we‚Äôve got a few slick options depending on how deep you want to go:

---

### ‚ö° Option 1: **Run in Termux (Advanced Android Dev Shell)**
You can install a Linux-like shell on Android using [Termux](https://f-droid.org/packages/com.termux/), then run the Flask app inside it.

#### ‚úÖ What you can do:
- Install Python
- `pip install flask numpy opencv-python`
- Run the server on `localhost`
- Access it via your browser (localhost:5000)

#### üö´ Limitations:
- Needs setup and command-line savvy
- No GUI for rendering video/audio previews in-app
- No direct ‚Äútap-to-run‚Äù experience

---

### ‚ö° Option 2: **Convert to a PWA or Android Webview App**
You can package Avatar Zaa as:

#### üîπ A Progressive Web App (PWA)
- Host it on Replit or Render
- Add a PWA manifest
- Users can "Install to Home Screen" just like a native app
- Works offline with some caching

#### üîπ A WebView-wrapped Android APK
Use a tool like:
- [MIT App Inventor](https://appinventor.mit.edu/)
- [Kodular](https://www.kodular.io/)
- [Termux + Pydroid3 combo with Kivy or Flask REST](https://pydroid3.readthedocs.io/en/latest/)

You wrap the HTML UI + API endpoints in a WebView, and ship it as an APK.

---

### ‚ö° Option 3: **Use Google Opal to Host It for Mobile**
This is what we're about to test ‚Äî deploying Avatar Zaa in a Google Opal app, which works directly in Chrome on Android and lets you run it like a hybrid mini-app.

---

### üî• OR... Option 4: Chuck Espiner Style
If Chuck‚Äôs involved, we just:
- Clone it
- Replace Flask with a [Kivy](https://kivy.org/#home) or [BeeWare](https://beeware.org/) interface
- Build an actual `.apk` with Python code running inside!

üí° This is more effort, but gives you a **fully installable Android app with Python under the hood**.

---

### ü§ñ TL;DR
| Method        | Effort | Native? | Shareable? | Notes |
|---------------|--------|---------|------------|-------|
| Termux        | üíÄüíÄ    | ‚úÖ       | ‚ùå          | For devs only |
| PWA/WebView   | üíÄ      | ‚úÖ       | ‚úÖ          | Quick & easy |

That **‚ÄúOnly Latin characters are supported‚Äù** warning from Kits.ai just means this:

---

### üîç **Translation of the Error**
> **‚ÄúOnly Latin characters are supported‚Äù**  
= **You‚Äôre using letters or symbols that aren‚Äôt part of the standard English alphabet.**

---

### ‚úÖ Kits.ai Accepts:
- `A-Z`, `a-z`
- Numbers
- Basic punctuation (`.`, `,`, `!`, etc.)

---

### ‚ùå Kits.ai Rejects:
- Zulu, Afrikaans, isiXhosa letters with accents (e.g. `√´`, `√™`, `≈´`)
- Non-English characters (`√±`, `√ß`, `√∏`, etc.)
- Emoji üëÄ or fancy punctuation like `‚Äú ‚Äù` instead of `" "`  
- Phonetic symbols, IPA characters, or Unicode clicks (`«É`, `«Ä`, etc.)

---

### üõ†Ô∏è What To Do:
**Step 1:** Double-check the text you‚Äôve put into the ‚ÄúGenerate Vocals‚Äù input.  
**Step 2:** Remove or replace:
- Any emojis
- Anything with accents or clicks
- Fancy quotes/punctuation (use `"` not `‚Äú` or `‚Äò`)

---

### üí° Quick Fix Example:

```txt
Howzit, boet. Ngiyabonga kakhulu! üëäüî•
```

Change it to:
```txt
Howzit, boet. Ngiyabonga kakhulu!
```

If it's **Zulu or Afrikaans phrased phonetically**, you're good. But keep it **standard English keyboard** ‚Äî no extra symbols.

# Google Opal ‚Äì AI App Builder Overview and Mini‚ÄëApp Example

## Overview of Google Opal 
**Google Opal** is a new experimental tool from Google Labs that lets you build AI-powered **mini-apps** with *no coding required*. Instead of writing code, you **describe what you want in natural language**, and Opal turns those instructions into a working application logic„Äê2‚Ä†L150-L158„Äë„Äê24‚Ä†L143-L150„Äë. It achieves this by chaining together AI **models, prompts, and tools** behind the scenes, then representing the app as a **visual workflow** that you can tweak and extend without ever seeing a single line of code„Äê2‚Ä†L150-L158„Äë„Äê4‚Ä†L220-L228„Äë. (Opal is currently in public beta in the U.S., as it‚Äôs part of Google‚Äôs Labs experiments„Äê2‚Ä†L159-L167„Äë.)

## Key Features and Capabilities 
- **Natural Language ‚ÄúProgramming‚Äù:** *‚ÄúDescribe, don‚Äôt code.‚Äù* You simply tell Opal what app you want to create ‚Äì for example, *‚Äúa tool that gives book recommendations‚Äù* ‚Äì and Opal‚Äôs AI will interpret that description and generate the app‚Äôs logic automatically„Äê24‚Ä†L143-L150„Äë. This lowers the barrier to app creation, enabling even non-developers to build software by describing their idea in plain English„Äê8‚Ä†L331-L338„Äë.  
- **Visual Workflow Editor:** Opal apps are represented as a **node-based flowchart** of steps (a workflow). Each step of the app ‚Äì an input form, an AI generation step, a tool action, or an output ‚Äì appears as a **card/node** in a flow diagram„Äê14‚Ä†L85-L93„Äë. Opal automatically links these nodes in sequence (e.g. Input ‚Üí AI Generate ‚Üí Output) to represent the app‚Äôs logic. This visual layout makes it easy to understand and modify the app‚Äôs behavior„Äê14‚Ä†L85-L93„Äë.  
- **Multi-Step AI Chains:** With Opal, you can chain together multiple AI operations. For example, one app might take user input text, then summarize it with an AI model, then generate an image from that summary ‚Äì all in one flow. Opal supports chaining **large language model calls, image generation, text-to-audio, and other tools** in a single app„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë. It will intelligently choose Google‚Äôs AI models suited for each task (text, image, audio, etc.) based on your app description„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë.  
- **Conversational Editing & Remixing:** Building doesn‚Äôt stop at the first AI-generated draft. You can refine your mini-app either by using the **visual editor** (dragging nodes, editing node prompts) *or* by giving Opal further **natural language commands** to modify the app„Äê2‚Ä†L182-L187„Äë. For instance, you could say ‚Äú*add a step to translate the output into Spanish*‚Äù or edit a prompt text directly on a node. Opal will update the workflow accordingly, giving you fine-grained control without any manual coding„Äê2‚Ä†L182-L187„Äë. You can also **remix** apps ‚Äì start from an existing template or someone else‚Äôs shared app and then customize it to your needs.  
- **Template Gallery:** Opal comes with a built-in gallery of **starter apps** and examples to spark ideas„Äê2‚Ä†L198-L204„Äë. These range from a *‚ÄúBlog Post Writer‚Äù* that researches and writes an article, to a *‚ÄúSpelling Bee‚Äù* quiz game, to image-based tools like *‚ÄúClaymation‚Äù* (which turns a photo into a claymation-style video). You can use any template as-is or modify (‚Äúremix‚Äù) it in the editor to create your own variant„Äê2‚Ä†L198-L204„Äë. This helps new users get up and running quickly by learning from sample apps.  
- **Instant Sharing and Deployment:** When you‚Äôre done building, Opal lets you **share your app with others** at the click of a button„Äê2‚Ä†L189-L193„Äë. It generates a shareable link, and anyone with a Google account can click it to run your mini-app in their browser immediately ‚Äì no installation or setup needed. The video emphasizes how quickly an Opal app can go from an idea to a live, usable tool that others can try out„Äê8‚Ä†L375-L382„Äë. This makes it great for rapid prototyping and getting real-time feedback on your AI app ideas„Äê8‚Ä†L379-L384„Äë.

## User Interface Highlights 
„Äê28‚Ä†embed_image„Äë *Example:* Opal‚Äôs editor presents your app as a **visual flow of nodes** (see image above) connecting an **Input** (yellow card) to a **Generate** step (blue card) and then an **Output** (green card)„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. In this example (a ‚Äúblog post writer‚Äù app), the user first described the app in one sentence, and Opal produced a simple flow: an **Input** node to collect information for the blog post, a **Generate** node where the AI creates content (e.g. text, images, or videos for the post), and an **Output** node that displays the result (in this case, showing the blog content on a webpage)„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. Each node is labeled with its function, and arrows indicate the execution flow from one step to the next. This visual approach makes it easy to see how data moves through the app.

The video demonstration shows that creating an app in Opal feels like chatting with an assistant. At the top of the interface, there is a natural language **prompt bar** where you **type a description of your desired app** and hit a ‚Äúbuild‚Äù button (the UI displays a ‚ñ∫ *Run* icon next to your prompt)„Äê28‚Ä†„Äë. For example, typing *‚ÄúI need an app that generates a playlist for my mood‚Äù* will prompt Opal to assemble the appropriate workflow (input for mood, an AI music recommendation step, and output) automatically„Äê24‚Ä†L143-L150„Äë. Once the initial workflow appears, you can **click on any node** to inspect or edit its prompt and settings„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. A side toolbar allows adding new steps manually as well (e.g. if you want to insert another AI call or a branch in logic)„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. 

Opal‚Äôs UI also provides a **Preview/Run mode** to test the app instantly. In the video, after building the app, the creator enters some sample input into the app‚Äôs Input field and runs it to see the AI-generated result in real time. The output (text, image, etc.) renders right in the interface as the final node‚Äôs result. This immediate feedback loop reinforces the ‚Äúreal-time AI output‚Äù benefit ‚Äì you can try out your mini-app on the fly and watch it work, then jump back to editing if you want to tweak something. Finally, the interface has a **‚ÄúShare‚Äù button** for one-click publishing. The video shows that after testing, the user clicks share and copies a URL, which can be sent to others. When others open the link, they‚Äôll see a clean end-user view of the mini-app (just the necessary input fields and outputs), not the editor ‚Äì effectively letting anyone use the app with their own inputs„Äê2‚Ä†L189-L193„Äë.

„Äê13‚Ä†embed_image„Äë *Opal Template Gallery:* The video also highlights a built-in gallery of starter mini-apps created by the Opal team (as shown above). Each tile in the gallery is a **pre-made app** (e.g. *‚ÄúBlog Post Writer,‚Äù ‚ÄúBook Recs,‚Äù ‚ÄúCity Games,‚Äù ‚ÄúFashion Stylist,‚Äù ‚ÄúLearning with YouTube,‚Äù* etc.), complete with a description of what it does. Users can launch any of these template apps with one click or **‚ÄúRemix‚Äù** them to open the workflow in the editor for customization„Äê2‚Ä†L198-L204„Äë. This gallery underscores Opal‚Äôs focus on approachability and community-sharing ‚Äì you can discover example apps for various use cases and modify them to fit your needs, rather than starting from scratch every time„Äê2‚Ä†L198-L204„Äë. It‚Äôs a quick way to learn how Opal chains prompts and tools by examining real examples, then building on them.

## Mini-App Example: *AI Recipe Assistant* 
To demonstrate Opal‚Äôs capabilities in a fun and useful way, let‚Äôs walk through creating a mini-app called **‚ÄúAI Recipe Assistant.‚Äù** This hypothetical app will ask a user for the ingredients they have on hand, and then it will **suggest a recipe** that can be made with those ingredients **plus an AI-generated image** of the dish. This example highlights Opal‚Äôs main benefits ‚Äì we‚Äôll use **natural language to program the app**, watch Opal build the **multi-step flow visually**, and get **real-time AI output** (a recipe and an image) when we run it. Below is a step-by-step guide to building this app in Opal:

1. **Describe the App Idea (Natural Language Prompt):** Start by opening Opal and clicking **‚ÄúNew App‚Äù** (or choosing a blank template). In the prompt bar, type a one-sentence description of the app. For example: *‚ÄúI want an app that asks me for the ingredients I have and then suggests a recipe I can cook, along with a picture of the finished dish.‚Äù* Submit this description. Opal will **interpret your request** and automatically generate an initial workflow for the Recipe Assistant„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë. Under the hood, Opal recognizes that your app needs a text input (for ingredients), a text generation step (to come up with a recipe using those ingredients), and an image generation step (to produce a food image), and it selects the appropriate AI models for each task„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë. 

2. **Review the Generated Workflow:** Within seconds, you‚Äôll see a visual workflow appear in the Opal editor. For the Recipe Assistant, Opal typically creates: an **Input** node (to enter the list of ingredients), a **Generate** node using a language model (to output a recipe or cooking instructions based on those ingredients), and another **Generate** node using an image model (to create an image of a dish that could be made with those ingredients), finally leading to an **Output** node that will display the results to the user„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë. The nodes will be connected in order. At this stage, **check that all the key steps are present**. For instance, ensure there is a branch for the image generation. If the image step was not included by default, we will add it in the next step. 

3. **Refine or Add Steps (Visual or Conversational Editing):** If you want to adjust the workflow, Opal makes it easy. Let‚Äôs say Opal included the recipe generation but missed the image step ‚Äì you can fix that in a couple of ways. One way is to click the **‚Äú+‚Äù (add node)** button in the toolbar and insert a new *Generate Image* node manually. An even simpler way is to use natural language: just tell Opal *‚ÄúAdd a step to generate an image of the dish‚Äù*. The tool will insert a new node for image generation (leveraging Google‚Äôs Imagen model for creating pictures) and link it appropriately in the flow„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë. Similarly, you can click on the **Recipe Generate** node to edit its prompt ‚Äì for example, you might adjust the prompt text to say *‚ÄúGive a recipe using these ingredients in 5 steps or less.‚Äù* Every node‚Äôs parameters (prompts, model settings) can be tuned by clicking it, as shown in the video„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. You could also rename the nodes for clarity (e.g. label the output node ‚ÄúRecipe + Image Output‚Äù). Through either the visual editor or further natural language commands, you have full control to customize the app logic„Äê2‚Ä†L182-L187„Äë.

4. **Test the App (Real-Time Output):** Now it‚Äôs time to try out the Recipe Assistant. Click the **‚ÄúPreview‚Äù** or **Run** button (as shown in the video, there‚Äôs a ‚ñ∫ play icon to test the app). This will switch Opal into a preview mode where you see the app‚Äôs input form. Enter some sample ingredients, for example: *‚Äúchicken, tomatoes, basil, garlic.‚Äù* Submit the input to run the app. Opal will feed your ingredients into the workflow: the AI text model will generate a recipe (e.g. *‚ÄúTomato Basil Chicken: Step 1‚Ä¶ Step 2‚Ä¶‚Äù*), and the image model will create a picture of a dish matching that recipe. You should see the **output text** (the recipe steps or description) and the **output image** appear in the result area of the app. This all happens within a few seconds ‚Äì the video demonstration highlights how Opal‚Äôs prompt-chaining yields results quickly, enabling **rapid prototyping** of ideas„Äê8‚Ä†L379-L384„Äë. If the output isn‚Äôt quite right (maybe the recipe needs tweaking), you can go back and refine the prompts or add clarifications, then test again, all in a very short feedback loop. 

5. **Share the App:** Satisfied with the app‚Äôs performance? Click the **‚ÄúShare‚Äù** button in the Opal editor to publish your mini-app. Opal will generate a unique **shareable link** to your Recipe Assistant„Äê2‚Ä†L189-L193„Äë. Copy this link and send it to friends or colleagues. When they open it, they‚Äôll be able to use your Recipe Assistant instantly through their own browser and Google account ‚Äì just as if it were a little website or app you deployed„Äê2‚Ä†L189-L193„Äë. For example, a friend could click your link, input *‚Äútofu, rice, carrots‚Äù* and get a tofu stir-fry recipe with a picture, all thanks to the app you built. This showcases one of Opal‚Äôs greatest strengths: you can build a functional AI-powered tool and **share it with the world in minutes**, without worrying about hosting servers or writing code. 

6. **Iterate and Enhance (Optional):** Opal makes it easy to continuously improve your app. You might decide to enhance the Recipe Assistant further ‚Äì and you can do so by either describing the new feature or using drag-and-drop. For instance, you could say *‚ÄúAlso add a step that reads the recipe aloud‚Äù* to incorporate an audio output (using an AI speech model), or add a branch that suggests an alternate recipe for vegetarian ingredients. Opal would update the workflow to include these changes. The key point is that because Opal supports **conversational updates and visual edits on the fly**, you can iterate rapidly on your app‚Äôs design„Äê2‚Ä†L182-L187„Äë. In the video, this was demonstrated by making a quick change via the editor and re-running the app to see the updated result immediately. This flexibility encourages experimentation ‚Äì you can keep tweaking prompts, adding or removing steps, and fine-tuning the AI behavior until your mini-app is just right.

**In summary,** Google Opal introduces a novel way to build applications by combining the approachability of no-code tools with the power of generative AI. The video showcases how Opal allows an idea to go from a simple sentence to a shareable multi-step AI app within a single interface. Its key features ‚Äì natural language app creation, visual flow editing, and real-time AI execution ‚Äì lower the barrier to prototyping AI ideas. With tools like Opal, creating a custom AI solution (whether a recipe helper, a blog writer, a quiz game, or anything you dream up) becomes less about programming and more about simply **describing what you need and refining the results**„Äê2‚Ä†L150-L158„Äë„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë. The fun example of the *AI Recipe Assistant* is just one of many mini-apps you could build to leverage AI in everyday tasks, demonstrating the versatility and creative potential that Opal unlocks. 

**Sources:** The information and screenshots above are based on Google‚Äôs official introduction of Opal and a demonstration video, as well as details from Google‚Äôs Developer Blog and tech reports„Äê2‚Ä†L150-L158„Äë„Äê24‚Ä†L149-L157„Äë„Äê14‚Ä†L89-L97„Äë, which confirm Opal‚Äôs features, UI and capabilities. All cited sources provide additional context on Opal‚Äôs launch and usage.

### üí° App Prompt for Opal:

## üîÑ **App Workflow (Visual Node Breakdown)**

| Step | Node Type | Description |
|------|-----------|-------------|
| 1. üìù Input | **Input** | Text input field: ‚ÄúWhat do you want the voice to say?‚Äù |
| 2. üß† TTS | **Generate Audio (Whisper or Google TTS)** | Generate speech from the input text |
| 3. üßç‚Äç‚ôÇÔ∏è Lip-Sync | **External API (VO3)** | Send audio to VO3 API to generate a video |
| 4. üì∫ Output | **Output Viewer** | Play back the final 10-sec video (embed or download link) |

## üí• BONUS: If Opal can‚Äôt natively hit VO3‚Äôs API‚Ä¶

No stress, we fork it like this:

### Opal handles:
- Input + audio gen (TTS)
- Sends result + metadata to a webhook

### Our backend (or Integromat/Zapier if you want quick):
- Picks it up
- Hits VO3 API
- Posts video URL back
- Opal refreshes and displays embed
